Since message_id is unique per message, this caused the system prompt to differ on every turn, busting prefix-based prompt caches on local model providers (llama-server, LM Studio/MLX) and causing full cache rebuilds on every conversation turn.\\n• Why it matters: Cache invalidation on every turn increases latency, costs, and reduces efficiency for local models.\\n• What changed: Moved per-message identifiers from buildInboundMetaSystemPrompt() (system prompt) to buildInboundUserContextPrefix() (user context prefix). System prompt now contains only session-stable routing fields.\\n• What did NOT change (scope boundary): Other metadata fields (sender info, thread starter, forwarded message, chat history) remain unchanged. The buildInboundMetaSystemPrompt() trusted metadata schema remains the same.\\n\\nChange Type\\n\\n• [x] Bug fix\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [X] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [ ] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [ ] Memory / storage\\n- [ ] Integrations\\n- [ ] API / contracts\\n- [ ] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #19892 , #19989\\n- Related #\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\nList user-visible changes (including defaults/config).  \\nIf none, write `None`.\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n* New permissions/capabilities? Gateway acknowledges with empty \\\"final\\\" event (model still processing)\\n3. `loadHistory()` clears chat log and reloads from server\\n4. User's message not yet in server history → disappears\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nSkip history reload when a local run ends with an empty final event but a **different** run is still active. implement Teams AI agent UX best practices\",\"body\":\"## Summary\\n\\nMigrates the Teams extension from `@microsoft/agents-hosting` to the official [Teams SDK](https://github.com/microsoft/teams-sdk) (`@microsoft/teams.apps` + `@microsoft/teams.api`) and implements [Microsoft's AI UX best practices](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoftteams/platform/bots/how-to/teams-conversational-ai/ai-ux) for Teams agents.\\n\\n### SDK Migration\\n\\n- Replace `@microsoft/agents-hosting` (CloudAdapter, MsalTokenProvider, authorizeJWT) with Teams SDK `App`, `Client`, and `JwtValidator`\\n- Custom lightweight adapter wrapping the Teams SDK REST client for proactive messaging, `updateActivity`, and `deleteActivity`\\n- JWT validation via `createServiceTokenValidator` from `@microsoft/teams.apps` (validates signature via JWKS, audience, issuer, expiration)\\n- Token factory pattern — each API call fetches a fresh token instead of caching a potentially stale value\\n- `User-Agent` header on all outbound HTTP requests\\n- Wire Teams `clientInfo` timezone into the agent system prompt\\n\\n### AI UX Features\\n\\n- **AI-generated label**: All outbound messages include the `AIGeneratedContent` entity and `channelData.feedbackLoopEnabled` so Teams renders the \\\\\\\"AI generated\\\\\\\" badge and native thumbs up/down UI\\n- **Streaming responses** (1:1 only): Uses the [Teams `streaminfo` entity protocol](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoftteams/platform/bots/streaming-ux) with `onPartialReply` to progressively update messages as the LLM generates tokens, throttled at 1.5s via the shared `draft-stream-loop`\\n- **Informative status updates**: Sends a randomized status message (e.g. \\\\\\\"Scuttling through ideas...\\\\\\\") immediately when a message arrives, showing a blue progress bar while the LLM processes\\n- **Typing indicators**: Only sent in group chats (Teams doesn't support them in channels; 1:1 uses streaming instead)\\n- **Welcome card**: Sends an Adaptive Card with configurable prompt starters when the bot is added to a 1:1 chat\\n- **Feedback with reflective learning**: Handles `message/submitAction` invoke for thumbs up/down. Negative feedback triggers a fire-and-forget background reflection — the agent reviews its response, derives a learning, and proactively messages the user with adjustments. Feedback events persisted as `type: \\\\\\\"custom\\\\\\\"` / `event: \\\\\\\"feedback\\\\\\\"` in session JSONL for mining\\n\\n### Infrastructure\\n\\n- `updateActivity` REST helper and `updateActivity` on `MSTeamsTurnContext` for streaming\\n- `invokeResponse` handling — no-op in custom adapter (HTTP 200 sent by `process()`)\\n- Stream fallback for long replies (\\u003e4000 chars) — falls through to chunked delivery\\n- Stream finalization for empty text (clears progress bar when agent sends a card via tool)\\n- Shared `AI_GENERATED_ENTITY` constant extracted to `ai-entity.ts`\\n- New config fields: `welcomeCard`, `promptStarters`, `groupWelcomeCard`, `feedbackEnabled`, `feedbackReflection`, `feedbackReflectionCooldownMs`\\n\\n### Bug Fix\\n\\n- **Copy-pasted image downloads**: Added `smba.trafficmanager.net` to `DEFAULT_MEDIA_AUTH_HOST_ALLOWLIST` — pasted images arrive via Bot Framework attachment URLs at this host and require the bot's Bearer token, which was previously not sent because the host was missing from the auth allowlist\\n\\n### Known Issues\\n\\n- Proactive send from DM may route to wrong conversation when user has multiple conversations (#51947)\\n\\nCloses #51806\\n\\n## Manual test evidence\\n\\nTested on Azure VM deployment with Teams Web. 29/30 tests passed, 0 failed, 1 not tested (group chat). For example, selecting DeepSeek from a session running on ZAI produces `zai/deepseek-chat` instead of `deepseek/deepseek-chat` — causing \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors.\\n\\nThis is the root cause behind 9+ independent bug reports across different provider combinations (ZAI/DeepSeek, Ollama/Moonshot, MiniMax/Kimi, etc.).\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\nThree call sites use `resolveServerChatModelValue(model, modelProvider)` which blindly prepends the session's current provider to the bare model name:\\n\\n1. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:542` — active session model display\\n2. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:549` — default model display\\n3. `ui/src/ui/chat/slash-command-executor.ts:158` — /model slash command\\n\\nThe `modelProvider` from the server reflects the **previous** model's provider, not the newly selected model's provider.\\n\\n## User impact\\n\\nEvery user who switches between models from different providers in the Control UI gets \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors. Affects all multi-provider setups.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nFor bare model names (no `/`), create a raw `ChatModelOverride` and resolve the correct provider through `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue()`, which looks up the model in the catalog and returns the catalog's provider. Falls back to server-provided provider only if catalog lookup fails.\\n\\nAll 3 call sites are fixed. 2 files, +30/-7.\\n\\n## How to verify\\n\\n1. Configure 2+ providers (e.g. ZAI + DeepSeek)\\n2. Start a session with one provider's model\\n3. Switch to another provider's model via UI dropdown\\n4. Before: \\\"model not allowed\\\". After: switches correctly.\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n`chat-model-ref.test.ts` covers `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` catalog lookup. The fix routes through this existing tested path. No new test needed — the functions are correct, only the call sites were wrong.\\n\\n🤖 Generated with [Claude When jiti\\nCJS-transforms the barrel, both star-exports call `Object.defineProperty`\\nfor the same property with `configurable: false`. The second call throws.\\n\\n## Why reordering `export *` does not fix it\\n\\njiti's `_exportNames` dedup guard only fires for symbols registered by\\nnamed exports. `export *` never populates `_exportNames`, so the guard\\nnever fires regardless of which star-export comes first.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nNamed pre-exports for all 15 symbols that `line-runtime.ts` re-exports\\nfrom this extension. #51824\\n\\n## Problem\\n\\nWhen switching models in the Control UI, the model picker sends the **wrong provider prefix**. For example, selecting DeepSeek from a session running on ZAI produces `zai/deepseek-chat` instead of `deepseek/deepseek-chat` — causing \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors.\\n\\nThis is the root cause behind 9+ independent bug reports across different provider combinations (ZAI/DeepSeek, Ollama/Moonshot, MiniMax/Kimi, etc.).\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\nThree call sites use `resolveServerChatModelValue(model, modelProvider)` which blindly prepends the session's current provider to the bare model name:\\n\\n1. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:542` — active session model display\\n2. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:549` — default model display\\n3. `ui/src/ui/chat/slash-command-executor.ts:158` — /model slash command\\n\\nThe `modelProvider` from the server reflects the **previous** model's provider, not the newly selected model's provider.\\n\\n## User impact\\n\\nEvery user who switches between models from different providers in the Control UI gets \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors. Affects all multi-provider setups.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nFor bare model names (no `/`), create a raw `ChatModelOverride` and resolve the correct provider through `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue()`, which looks up the model in the catalog and returns the catalog's provider. Falls back to server-provided provider only if catalog lookup fails.\\n\\nAll 3 call sites are fixed. 2 files, +30/-7.\\n\\n## How to verify\\n\\n1. Configure 2+ providers (e.g. ZAI + DeepSeek)\\n2. Start a session with one provider's model\\n3. Switch to another provider's model via UI dropdown\\n4. Before: \\\"model not allowed\\\". After: switches correctly.\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n`chat-model-ref.test.ts` covers `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` catalog lookup. The fix routes through this existing tested path. No new test needed — the functions are correct, only the call sites were wrong.\\n\\n🤖 Generated with [Claude                                                                                                                                                                                                             \\r\\n   \\r\\n  - Problem: normalizeSlug in src/agents/skills-clawhub.ts only rejected path-traversal characters (/, \\\\, ..) but accepted arbitrary Unicode, allowing Cyrillic homograph slugs (e.g., reаct with U+0430) to pass validation as distinct slugs visually identical to legitimate ones.                                                                       \\r\\n  - Why it matters: An attacker could register a visually identical skill slug on ClawHub to impersonate a popular skill, enabling phishing or supply-chain confusion when users install skills by name.\\r\\n  - What changed: normalizeSlug now lowercases input and enforces /^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]*$/, rejecting any non-ASCII character. Seven new test cases cover Cyrillic, CJK, Arabic, and malformed slugs.                                                                                                                                                         \\r\\n  - What did NOT change (scope boundary): No changes to ClawHub API contracts, gateway RPC handlers, CLI argument parsing, or any other slug consumer.
